<div id="review_521987362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521987362" />
    <a title="Loraine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7974251-loraine"><img alt="Loraine" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521987362?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loraine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loraine" href="/user/show/7974251-loraine">Loraine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521987362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5831339557625030989">I read two different editions of Salten's <i>Bambi</i>, the first a Pocket Edition published in 1942. The statement after the foreword, which is written by John Galsworthy, added the ephemera of time to my reading: [In order to cooperate with the government's war effort, this book has been made in strict conformity with WPB regulations restricting the use of certain materials.] The accession date of the second book is 1988, and is a hard cover copy with beautiful drawings by Kurt Wiese, a German by bir</span>
  <span id="freeText5831339557625030989" style="display:none">I read two different editions of Salten's <i>Bambi</i>, the first a Pocket Edition published in 1942. The statement after the foreword, which is written by John Galsworthy, added the ephemera of time to my reading: [In order to cooperate with the government's war effort, this book has been made in strict conformity with WPB regulations restricting the use of certain materials.] The accession date of the second book is 1988, and is a hard cover copy with beautiful drawings by Kurt Wiese, a German by birth who immigrated to the United States in 1927. The translator for both editions is Whittaker Chambers (literally, a spy who came in out of the cold).<br /><br />I never read Bambi as a youngster. Of course, I saw the movie, but Walt Disney created a confection, a mere froth, out of a stunning book. I knew something was up when I read about Felix Salten in <i>The Lady in Gold: The Extraordinary Tale of Gustav Klimt's Masterpiece, Portrait of Adele Bloch-Bauer</i>. Just the fact that he rubbed elbows with the likes of Gustav Klimt as he socialized with the literati at the Viennese salons of the intelligentsia clued me in. <br /><br />First of all, there's no Thumper! Keep that in mind. There's no Thumper. There <u>is</u> Old Hare, and he's a much more distinguished creature. This is a lyrical description of the natural world--albeit unsentimental, even brutal. The web of life is very unforgiving of the maimed, the weak, and the old. But the observations about the natural world, the changing of the seasons, the behaviors of the creatures, his narrative provokes powerful images in the reader's mind. <br /><br />The hunt, with beaters driving the animals towards The Man, with his friends and their loaded guns, is horrific. The building tension leading to the slaughter (for what, the sake of the "sport"?) is so fraught that the narration overwhelms the reader's senses. The Nazis banned the book in 1936, in part because they claimed the hunt was a subversive reference to the treatment of Jews, but Salten was Jewish and this was just one more brutal ploy on the road of genocide. And in America, The American Rifleman's Association opposed the Disney movie's depiction of hunters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5831339557625030989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9062715409036638809">Read my original review at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://merikthorne.blogspot.com/2016/12/bambi-by-felix-salten-tale-of-young.html'>http://merikthorne.blogspot.com/2016/...</a>.<br/><br/>I'm quite the fan of Walt Disney's interpretation of <i>Bambi</i>, but was rather hesitant to hear the original tale, due to the many mentionings of its harshness towards the practice of hunting. Yet I was surprised to find that it was not a disappointment!<br/><br/>Felix Salten's <i>Bambi</i> is the tale of a young stag and the future prince of the forest. Hidden deep in the woods with his mother, he watches as his animal friends grow and explore. Al</span>
  <span id="freeText9062715409036638809" style="display:none">Read my original review at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://merikthorne.blogspot.com/2016/12/bambi-by-felix-salten-tale-of-young.html">http://merikthorne.blogspot.com/2016/...</a>.<br /><br />I'm quite the fan of Walt Disney's interpretation of <i>Bambi</i>, but was rather hesitant to hear the original tale, due to the many mentionings of its harshness towards the practice of hunting. Yet I was surprised to find that it was not a disappointment!<br /><br />Felix Salten's <i>Bambi</i> is the tale of a young stag and the future prince of the forest. Hidden deep in the woods with his mother, he watches as his animal friends grow and explore. All the while, an unknown danger stalks their forest...<br /><br />I personally do not believe that killing wild animals for survival is wrong. However, I do agree with the book's point that killing off does and fawns disrupts the deer population more than the killing of stags.<br /><br />As to the book rather than the theme, itself: Though I listened to the audiobook instead of reading the actual story, the writing still came across as direct and only slightly descriptive, but still elegant with that old-fashioned flair.<br /><br />The plot didn't seem to be entirely there; however, Bambi and his family were interesting enough to let the story flow along on their own.<br /><br />In the end, <i>Bambi</i> made for a charming (if sad) little story. I wouldn't recommend it to children or tweens, -- mainly because of how it portrays mankind as evil -- but it is a somewhat peaceful tale.<br /><br />You may want to know: Several characters are killed.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1954872078&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954872078" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer145105674386482107">The reasons why this book is so sad:<br/><br/>1. No one gets over Gobo's death which makes everyone all sad and unhappy.<br/><br/>2. Bambi doesn't even know if he loves Faline anymore.<br/><br/>3. Faline is feeling so droopy and depressed that if she were a human she'd probably kill herself.<br/><br/>4. The old stag dies just when things get worse.<br/><br/>5. Bambi has so many happy memories of when he was little that you wish he'd never gotten older in the first place.<br/> <br/><br/> So, for the most part this book is the sad one while the sequel is the ha</span>
  <span id="freeText145105674386482107" style="display:none">The reasons why this book is so sad:<br /><br />1. No one gets over Gobo's death which makes everyone all sad and unhappy.<br /><br />2. Bambi doesn't even know if he loves Faline anymore.<br /><br />3. Faline is feeling so droopy and depressed that if she were a human she'd probably kill herself.<br /><br />4. The old stag dies just when things get worse.<br /><br />5. Bambi has so many happy memories of when he was little that you wish he'd never gotten older in the first place.<br /> <br /><br /> So, for the most part this book is the sad one while the sequel is the happier one</span>
  <a data-text-id="145105674386482107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9641984186746405463" style="display:none">ENGLISH: This is the fourth time I've read "Bambi," which is one of my 50 favorite books of all time.<br /><br />The Disney movie does not differ much from Salten's novel, on the contrary, it is notoriously true to the book, and includes many scenes almost to the letter. <div id="review_3250106671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3250106671" />
    <a title="John_Dishwasher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44246464-john-dishwasher"><img alt="John_Dishwasher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543641832p2/44246464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3250106671?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John_Dishwasher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John_Dishwasher" href="/user/show/44246464-john-dishwasher">John_Dishwasher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780685284476" href="/book/show/35379358-bambi">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44246464-john-dishwasher?shelf=public-domain">public-domain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44246464-john-dishwasher?shelf=short-novels">short-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3250106671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4348980102083654374">This book is meant to introduce children to the concepts of danger and death, I think. It is laudable that Salten is able to imbue almost every scene here with either foreboding or dread or some grisly death, and yet keep the storytelling mostly light and playful. He also leaves the message that the wisest among us are those who can manage danger and death without sacrificing their dignity. <br/><br/>At times, especially when the animals were reflecting on the dangers of human beings, the book reminded me</span>
  <span id="freeText4348980102083654374" style="display:none">This book is meant to introduce children to the concepts of danger and death, I think. It is laudable that Salten is able to imbue almost every scene here with either foreboding or dread or some grisly death, and yet keep the storytelling mostly light and playful. He also leaves the message that the wisest among us are those who can manage danger and death without sacrificing their dignity. <br /><br />At times, especially when the animals were reflecting on the dangers of human beings, the book reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76620.Watership_Down__Watership_Down___1_" title="Watership Down (Watership Down, #1) by Richard Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Watership Down</a>, by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7717.Richard_Adams" title="Richard Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Adams</a>, though I suppose any group of non-human animals discussing human beings would engage in the same kinds of dire conversations, which would explain the parallels. Salten is not shy about portraying humans as the ultimate predator, even a <i>betrayer</i> of nature. This seems to me ahead of its time for a popular book of 1920s America.<br /><br />Occasionally Salten’s childlike tone feels a little overripe, but I think this is probably a generational bias. Contemporary storytellers for youth seem to leave out his subtly patronizing lilt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4348980102083654374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=animal-story">animal-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=pick-a-shelf">pick-a-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=play-book-tag">play-book-tag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=animal">animal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1793244538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer270691203950571928">The last time I read this I was a child--I liked it back then but am not sure if I fell in love with it; I didn't fall in love with it now, either. I think my sister's audio recording of the Disney version may have spoiled it a bit for me, but I'm not sure. It's a bit dated, and, frankly, I read more than one book about wild animals and their fear of Man growing up. It's almost like Bambi doesn't have a well developed POV--he seems a bit detached from everything and everyone, which is what keeps</span>
  <span id="freeText270691203950571928" style="display:none">The last time I read this I was a child--I liked it back then but am not sure if I fell in love with it; I didn't fall in love with it now, either. I think my sister's audio recording of the Disney version may have spoiled it a bit for me, but I'm not sure. It's a bit dated, and, frankly, I read more than one book about wild animals and their fear of Man growing up. It's almost like Bambi doesn't have a well developed POV--he seems a bit detached from everything and everyone, which is what keeps me from liking this more than three stars. Or it could be the voicing, the writing, I don't know what, but it falls short for me and pulls this classic down.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="270691203950571928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1179540381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179540381" />
    <a title="Lacey Louwagie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33816-lacey-louwagie"><img alt="Lacey Louwagie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330366315p2/33816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179540381?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lacey Louwagie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lacey Louwagie" href="/user/show/33816-lacey-louwagie">Lacey Louwagie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/6238604-bambi">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33816-lacey-louwagie?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33816-lacey-louwagie?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33816-lacey-louwagie?shelf=into-the-forest-2015">into-the-forest-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33816-lacey-louwagie?shelf=100-book-challenge-2015">100-book-challenge-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33816-lacey-louwagie?shelf=disney-movies">disney-movies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179540381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16820020704103088978">I never thought that a book about a deer in the woods could be such a page-turner.<br/><br/>One of my friends described the book as beautiful. Another told me it was "quite good." And I first came across it referenced in a YA book when I was in middle school, in which the narrator claimed it was much better than the Disney version. <br/><br/>I agree with all of the above.<br/><br/>I first quickly flipped through to make sure that the animals actually talked, since I have a hard time making it through books without any dialog</span>
  <span id="freeText16820020704103088978" style="display:none">I never thought that a book about a deer in the woods could be such a page-turner.<br /><br />One of my friends described the book as beautiful. Another told me it was "quite good." And I first came across it referenced in a YA book when I was in middle school, in which the narrator claimed it was much better than the Disney version. <br /><br />I agree with all of the above.<br /><br />I first quickly flipped through to make sure that the animals actually talked, since I have a hard time making it through books without any dialog. They do, and their discussion characterizes their individual species well. I loved the kindness and respect with which the animals seemed to treat one another by default, humoring one another's weaknesses and foibles. At the same time, there is an undercurrent of the danger and harshness of the natural world, as birds and smaller rodents are occasionally killed by fox and ferrets.<br /><br />But the main point of tension comes between those who live in the forest and the humans who encroach upon their very lives. The human threat looms much larger in this book than it does in the movie; the scene in which Bambi's mother is shot is a virtual blood bath, harrowing in its sense of entrapment. Indeed, it reminded me of a war story in which the enemy's soldiers had discovered and surrounded your hideout. Perhaps it is because of this harsh reality that Bambi's father instills in him the ideal that the only way to remain safe is to be alone:<br /><br />"But of all his teachings this had been the most important; you must live alone, if you wanted to preserve yourself, if you understood existence, if you wanted to attain wisdom, you had to live alone."<br /><br />Which is quite different from the overall feeling one takes away from the Disney movie, which is filled with cheerful sidekicks and the theme that "love is a song that never ends."<br /><br />This sense of aloneness permeates the book and is perhaps the most heartbreaking aspect of it. We see Faline's pain and confusion when Bambi decides, after a heady courtship, that he's "not sure" if he loves her anymore. We see Gobo's naivete when he returns from the human world believing that he has nothing to fear from it -- and the way this sets him apart from the other deer, so that he is no longer really one of them or truly domestic. One of the most poignant scenes in the book is one in which a fox tries to convince a hunting dog that he has become a traitor by allying himself with the humans; the dog's insistence that the human is the bringer of all good things, and that he is not alone in his decision to cross over to his side.<br /><br />There's also a quiet spirituality about the piece, as Bambi's father tells him that there is "another" who is higher than both humans and the forest creatures. <br /><br />I found this book at a library booksale and probably paid a quarter for it. I didn't know until I read it this weekend what a treasure I had on my bookshelf. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16820020704103088978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Morgan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366675-morgan"><img alt="Morgan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590151183p2/7366675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144546395?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/7366675-morgan">Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442467453" href="/book/show/15801402-bambi">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Morgan by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7370602-samuel">Samuel</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144546395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13204031598283541021">You would think because this is a movie more people would have read it, but try finding someone who even knows about the existence of this book. Like most Disney movies, this is not really the same story. Disney kept the environmental themes, but took out the philosophy and changed most of the names. For a children's book, this book is deep. There are a lot of philosophical type of moments that make you think about life, death, and nature around you. At times it's makes you smile and other times</span>
  <span id="freeText13204031598283541021" style="display:none">You would think because this is a movie more people would have read it, but try finding someone who even knows about the existence of this book. Like most Disney movies, this is not really the same story. Disney kept the environmental themes, but took out the philosophy and changed most of the names. For a children's book, this book is deep. There are a lot of philosophical type of moments that make you think about life, death, and nature around you. At times it's makes you smile and other times you might get depressed, kind of like how seasons change. If you seen the movie I recommend this book. Chances are it's not the book you think you're going to read, it's better.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('asQRo5BohOpgbEHurjYNy0N6IsUcRNzO8H5EKqXwkjNQliqdA6qHeed290Y5qgMiKZyZwqhq+O0zddJ2ca/1eQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gOL25WEY95TIUJXSBcn6hMxrACowUEhd8pn3kJJsyM66sM3b8tr0B09KI3qSVfRtpo27LYR+bH4xkmHMRjOvhA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Even Mildred Mayhew, whom I had hitherto regarded as my life\'s light, became less luminous. I was not engaged to Mildred, but I lodged with her mother, and I sang duets with Mildred and gave her gloves when it would run to it, which was seldom. She was a dear, good girl, and I meant to marry her some day. It is very nice to feel that a good little woman is thinking of you -- it helps you in your work -- and it is pleasant to know she will say &quot;Yes,&quot; when you say, &quot;Will you?&quot; But my legacy almost put Mildred out of my head, especially as she was staying with friends in the country. Before the gloss was off my new mourning, I was seated in my aunt\'s armchair in front of the fire in the drawing-room of my own house. My own house! It was grand, but rather lonely. I did think of Mildred just then. The room was comfortably furnished with rosewood and damask. On the walls hung a few fairly good oil paintings, but the space above the mantelpiece was disfigured by an exceedingly bad print, &quot;The Trial of Lord William Russell,&quot; framed in a dark frame. I got up to look at it. I had visited my aunt with dutiful regularity, but I never remembered seeing this frame before. It was not intended for a print, but for an oil-painting. It was of fine ebony, beautifully and curiously carved. I looked at it with growing interest, and when my aunt\'s housemaid -- I had retained her modest staff of servants -- came in with the lamp, I asked her how long the print had been there. &quot;Mistress only bought it two. days before she was took ill,&quot; she said; &quot;but the frame -- she didn\'t want to buy a new one -- so she got this out of the attic.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/262262.Felix_Salten">About Felix Salten</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17649496643182012174"><i>There is more than one author with this Name.</i><br/><br/>Felix Salten was an Austrian writer. He was born Siegmund Salzmann in Budapest, Hungary. When he was three weeks old, his family moved to Vienna, Austria. Many Jews were immigrating into the city in the late 19th century because Vienna had finally granted full citizenship to Jews in 1867.<br/><br/>When his father went bankrupt, Felix had to quit school and begin </span>
  <span id="freeText17649496643182012174" style="display:none"><i>There is more than one author with this Name.</i><br /><br />Felix Salten was an Austrian writer. He was born Siegmund Salzmann in Budapest, Hungary. When he was three weeks old, his family moved to Vienna, Austria. Many Jews were immigrating into the city in the late 19th century because Vienna had finally granted full citizenship to Jews in 1867.<br /><br />When his father went bankrupt, Felix had to quit school and begin working in an insurance agency. He also began submitting poems and book reviews to journals. He became part of the Young Vienna movement (Jung Wien) and soon received work as a full-time art and theater critic in the Vienna press. In 1901 he founded Vienna's first, short-lived literary cabaret. In 1900 he published his first collection of short stories. He was soon publishing, on an average, one book a year, of plays, short stories, novels, travel books, and essay collections. He also wrote for nearly all the major newspapers of Vienna. He wrote film scripts and librettos for operettas. In 1927 he became president of the Austrian P.E.N. club.<br /><br />His most famous work is <i>Bambi</i>, which he wrote in 1923. It was translated into English in 1928 and became a Book-of-the-Month Club hit. In 1933, he sold the film rights to Sidney Franklin for $1,000, who later transferred the rights to the Walt Disney studios. Disney released its movie based on <i>Bambi</i> in 1942.<br /><br />Life in Austria became perilous for a prominent Jew in the 1930s. Adolf Hitler had Salten's books banned in 1936. Two years later (1938), after Austria had become part of Germany, Salten moved to Zurich, Switzerland, where he lived until his death.<br /><br />He was married to the actress Ottilie Metzl, and had two children: Paul and Anna-Katherina. He wrote another book based on the character Bambi, titled <i>Bambi's Children: The Story of a Forest Family</i>, 1939. His stories "Perri" and "The Hound of Florence" inspired the Disney films <i>Perri</i> and <i>The Shaggy Dog</i>.<br /><br />Salten is considered to be the author of the erotic novel <i>Josephine Mutzenbacher</i>, the fictional autobiography of a Vienna prostitute, which was published in 1906.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17649496643182012174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Felix Salten wrote Bambi: A Li<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11612718282766406414\" style=\"display:none\">He came into the world in the middle of the thicket, in one of those little, hidden forest glades which seem to be entirely open but are really screened in on all sides. So begins one of the most beloved nature stories. Felix Salten wrote Bambi: A Life in the Woods in 1923. It was translated into English in 1928, becoming a Book-of-the-Month Club hit. Though not originally written for children, the film rights were sold to the Walt Disney studios and the animated movie was released in 1942. Taken directly from the first chapter of Salten\'s original tale, Bambi\'s First Day depicts the early moments of the fawn\'s life in the safety of a forest glen and the shelter of his mother\'s embrace.
